“Whoever seeks awakening,<br>Should cultivate this absorption.<br>Whoever has cultivated this absorption<br>Will be exalted in learning.

“For whoever has cultivated this absorption<br>And for whoever will cultivate it,<br>I cannot say that the heap of their merit<br>Has any limit.

“The merit from cultivating this absorption<br>Is abundant.<br>It increases knowledge,<br>While offering to the buddhas is not like that.

“Honoring with flowers, fragrances, garlands,<br>Food, drinks,<br>And utensils<br>Is not honoring the buddhas.

“Dṛḍhamati, whoever connects with the Dharma—<br>The Dharma realized by me<br>At the seat of awakening—<br>Honors the buddhas. ^F225b

“Whoever pursues that Dharma<br>And wants to behold buddhas<br>Should immediately pursue this absorption—<br>Precisely this kind of Dharma.

“Whoever engenders sublime joy<br>Based on having attained this absorption<br>Has previously known<br>Many thousands of buddhas.”

“Furthermore, Dṛḍhamati, in order to swiftly actualize the superknowledges, one should eagerly undertake the worship, restoration, and cleansing of stūpas. For, Dṛḍhamati, any noble son or daughter who cleans a stūpa of the thus-gone ones will acquire four pristine, excellent aspirations. What are those four aspirations? They are the pristine, excellent aspiration for one’s form; the pristine, excellent aspiration for perfect leisure; the pristine, excellent aspiration for the stability of one’s vows; and the pristine, excellent aspiration for beholding thus-gone ones.

“The accomplishment of [n87] virtuously engendering aspirations<br>Is that thus-gone ones will emerge,<br>Just as emanations emerge<br>Through the discernment of apprehending. [n88]

“Wheels on the soles of the feet and below the toes<br>Will appear among their marks.<br>I will explain such a sublime confluence of features as this,<br>So listen carefully!

“My marks are likewise perfectly apparent;<br>They are evenly distributed on my fingers and toes.<br>Perfectly exalted and evenly distributed,<br>Their distribution is extremely exalted.

“The luminosity of my marks is exalted,<br>And shines like ten million light rays.<br>Standing flooded with light, like Mount Meru,<br>My body is crowned with a net of light rays.

“On those marks, which embody the essence,<br>One hundred million light rays are present.<br>The names of each of them are different,<br>And so is their luminosity and color.

“From one of my light rays another thousand lights emerge,<br>Which are all present in multiple colors.<br>They will perform the deeds of awakened ones,<br>Even after the earth throughout the trichiliocosm has collapsed.

“I was born from the light of awakening;<br>I did not come from the fruition of actions.<br>Upon seeing the light of thus-gone ones,<br>Men and women become intoxicated.

“Thus-gone ones will manifest for many tens of millions of eons,<br>Or in the arrays of different buddha realms.<br>Wherever I performed awakened deeds,<br>Victorious ones will likewise manifest miraculous displays. ^F226a

“My absorption is all-illuminating;<br>It fully illuminates buddha realms.<br>The so-called luminous banner of Meru is exalted,<br>And the absorption called valiant progress is exalted.

“Among those with an all-pervasive vision of phenomena,<br>Some pristine ones will see buddhas manifesting here.<br>Some will see them entering the womb, being born,<br>And fearlessly and audaciously taking seven steps here.

“Thinking, ‘The victorious one will awaken to buddhahood,’<br>They will see buddhas seated in awakening at the center of the earth.<br>Some will think they will turn the wheel of Dharma.<br>Some will think they will act for the sake of awakening. [n89]

“Look at the radiance of that absorption,<br>Which produces these miraculous displays!<br>Some will think that my life span is an eon.<br>Some, however, will think it is half an eon.

“Then, some will think it is an intermediate eon—<br>Others, that it is two, three, four, or more eons.<br>Then, some will think that it is ten million years,<br>And some will fully see the actual length.

“Humans will perceive that my life span<br>In this Jampudvīpa is eighty years.<br>Some will perceive my life span to be a day and a night;<br>Some will perceive my life span to be long.

“Still others will think that it is like a day and a night<br>For the gods in this trichiliocosm.<br>Beings will understand precisely according to their inclinations,<br>And oral instructions will be dispensed to them accordingly.

“They will likewise by transformed according to their inclinations,<br>As wisdom is likewise taught to them accordingly.<br>Through being so taught, their interest will be aroused—<br>This is the marvel of the supernatural powers.

“If their own state of being were revealed,<br>Unwise people would go mad.<br>Who would not be gladdened<br>Upon seeing what my experience and state of being are?

“Those who have understood my experience<br>Will turn the wheel of Dharma.<br>Yet when preaching the Dharma for a variety of inclinations,<br>They will not fully understand my experience.

“Those who do not understand the experience of the omniscient<br>Will only teach a few expressions of Dharma.<br>Seeing that they have no perception whatsoever,<br>Their minds will be damaged.

“Those who understand the reality of the thus-gone ones<br>Are never mentally damaged.<br>They all adhere to such an experience<br>Of the sameness of phenomena. ^F226b

“Except for these eight monks<br>Who are seated in front of me with palms joined,<br>There will never be anyone here in the future, Dṛḍhamati,<br>To uphold this sūtra.

“Dṛḍhamati, they have continually partaken<br>Of the incomparable experience of past buddhas.<br>They have always approached,<br>Being vessels for the Dharma.

“They fully took on the mind of awakening,<br>And were continually praised by buddhas.<br>I know that just as they sit before me,<br>So too did they in the past.

“They have sat in the presence of as many victorious ones<br>As there are grains of sand in the river Ganges.<br>They will be present later, in the final five hundred years of the Dharma,<br>When I too will uphold that supreme awakening.

“In later times, the wisdom of the victorious ones will be theirs,<br>And you too, Dṛḍhamati, will be courageous in it.<br>There will also be eight million other heroes<br>Who will set out to uphold all teachings.

“I too will listen to the Dharma there.<br>Having heard it, I will abide by the Dharma,<br>Practicing it without respite.<br>Then I will teach it.

“And by teaching it, I will prophesy supreme awakening.<br>Upon hearing their own predictions given,<br>May the eight million be filled with joy,<br>And levitate to a height of seven palm trees.”

The Savior of the World then said to Ānanda,<br>“Would you be delighted and able<br>To uphold this Dharma<br>For the wicked in the future?”

“I would not be so delighted,” he said to the Blessed One.<br>The victorious one then knowingly said to Kāśyapa,<br>“Kāśyapa, will you uphold this Dharma?<br>You should uphold the Dharma once I have passed!”

“I would not delight in doing so,” said Kāśyapa.<br>“This trichiliocosm upholds all people,<br>Oceans, mountains, and forests,<br>And delights in bearing many other loads besides.

“But I would not delight in carrying this load.<br>Who will uphold the Dharma in the future?<br>It would be very difficult for me [n90] to control the monks.<br>As they will not abide by this teaching, ^F227a

“There is no need to mention that the guide of the world will have passed beyond.<br>They will say, ‘Kāśyapa, you have become too old,’<br>And so, in the future, my words will not be followed.<br>They will not abide by my teachings.

“Thinking, ‘We are adept in this and reflect on its meaning,’<br>They will reflect upon poetics and materialism,<br>And likewise adhere to mundane grammar.<br>Discarding concentration and absorption,

“They cavort with the worldly.<br>They will be prosperous and widely renowned,<br>And continually regarded by the world.<br>I could never examine them,

“And I see severe problems.<br>While I was dwelling alone in the forest,<br>A god appeared and said to me,<br>‘The victorious ones have taught such a Dharma.

“ ‘Many beings have been tamed in the Dharma of the noble ones.<br>Monks have become adept in concentration and absorption,<br>And perfected the liberations, miraculous abilities, and powers.<br>Hearing this, Śakra will be pleased.

“ ‘How amazing this is today!’<br>Later he will come to me,<br>And crying unhappily, declare,<br>‘Kāśyapa, the Dharma will soon disappear.’

“Hearing that I will be upset,<br>And not be eager to teach much.<br>I am not eager to uphold that sūtra,<br>For the monks will cower before it.

“They will not be pleased with the supreme speech,<br>And then the divine assembly will gather there.”<br>The Blessed One said to Kāśyapa,<br>“I already knew, Kāśyapa, that the way of Dharma cannot be upheld.

“There is no one here among my hearers<br>Who will uphold such sūtras as that.<br>Except for those authorized by me<br>To uphold such sūtras,

“Those who will later have no doubt,<br>Will have had their doubts resolved by me.<br>Why have those sūtras, more powerful than others,<br>Never before been practiced?

“The monks who uphold them are new and young,<br>While the sūtras are extensive.<br>How will those who do not uphold such a Dharma<br>Reach its other shore?

“Dṛḍhamati, those who see me today<br>While I teach<br>Will, in future times of great peril,<br>Acquire joy upon hearing that Dharma. ^F227b

“I have explained only apprehension.<br>The fearless should have faith in those words of mine.<br>Those who have seen the teacher in this life<br>Will be delighted to uphold that Dharma.

“They will pursue such wisdom<br>And then make offerings to the guides.<br>They will worship relics and memorials too;<br>The fearless will act as such at that time.”

Ānanda then rose from his seat, draped his shawl over one shoulder, knelt on his right knee and asked the Blessed One, “Blessed One, what is the name of this Dharma discourse? How will it be upheld?”

The Blessed One said to the venerable Ānanda, “Ānanda, you should uphold this Dharma discourse as Upholding the Roots of Virtue. You should also uphold it as Foundation of the Collection of Merit, or Aid to the Bodhisattvas, or The Inquiry Posed by the Bodhisattvas, or The Chapter that Resolves All Doubts.”

After the Blessed One thus spoke, the venerable Ānanda, the bodhisattva Dṛḍhamati, the other bodhisattvas, the great hearers, and the world with its gods, humans, demigods, and gandharvas were all pleased and praised what the Blessed One had said.

Translated by the Indian preceptor Prajñāvarman and the translator Bandé Leki Dé, then revised and finalized by the Indian preceptors Prajñāvarman and Jñānagarbha, and the chief editor-translator Bandé Yeshé Dé.


## Notes (84000)

[n1] Or Kumbhīra, as attested by Edgerton in his Buddhist Hybrid Sanskrit Dictionary and by the Chinese 金毘羅 (Soothill-Hodous), although both sources list this figure as a yakṣa or a nāga rather than a monk disciple of the Buddha.

[n2] The name Vasiṣṭha is based on the Chinese, 婆私 (Soothill-Hodous). The Tibetan reads thang la gnas/gnas pa.

[n3] S: lhas mchod; D: las mchod. The Chinese confirms with 天敬. The back-translation of Marutpūjita is from Chandra Das.

[n4] “Basis of worship,” here and throughout this passage, renders the Tibetan term mchod rten, which can render the Sanskrit stūpa or caitya. The Chinese has 塔廟, which typically renders stūpa.

[n5] Tentative translation. D: ji ltar mkha’ la nam yang lag pa mi thogs dang // rdul dang du ba rnams kyis gos par mi ’gyur dang // ji ltar lam ni nam yang byed par mi ’gyur ba // chos la de bzhin mos pa rnams ni dge sbyong yin. The corresponding Chinese verse reads: “Just as space is unobstructed and cannot be sullied by smoke or dust, so is the Dharma of the mendicant originally pure and unalterable (如空無障礙，煙塵不能污，沙門法如是，本淨無變異。).

[n6] Tentative translation. D: ji ltar sangs rgyas spyan mchog gis // khams gsum shes la ma chags ’jug pa bzhin // dngos dang dngos med mnyam tshungs yid dang ldan // yang dag brtson zhing rang gi mig la gnas // gang tshe rgyal ba ting ’dzin der gnas te // de ring de dag kun gyis thob snyam bgyid. The Chinese reads: “With a mind of equanimity regarding existence and nonexistence / you have thus attained the buddha eye, which can see everywhere throughout the three realms without hindrance. Because the Buddha has entered this absorption, it has caused us too to attain this eye” (等心於有無，因是得佛眼，能於三界中，普見無障礙。佛入三昧故，令我得是眼).

[n7] Tentative translation. D: rim par phye ba’i tshigs.

[n8] It is not obvious from the text how the many flowers come about. Perhaps the original flower is instantly multiplied. The Chinese is likewise confusing: “Then all the bodhisattvas wished to scatter this utpala flower throughout the ten directions, and the Buddha touched each flower with his hand and a complete buddha body appeared at the center of each” (時諸菩薩 以此蓮華欲散十方，佛以手摩一一華中佛 身悉現).

[n9] Ajita is another name for the bodhisattva Maitreya.

[n10] Tentative translation. D: mig yor gyi gnas la ’jig rten mi gnas te / ’phags pa rnams dang tha mi dad pa’i slad du’o.

[n11] This is a somewhat tentative translation. D reads: de dag gis rnam par mi rtog cig kun nas nyon mongs pa med la / snang ba med pa’i byang chub lam zhugs pa’i de bzhin gshegs pa rnams kyi de bzhin gshegs pa’i gter dang / chos kyi gter bstan pa’i chos kyi rnam grangs de thos nas skrag cing dngang la dngang bar ’gyur zhing g.yang sa chen por yang ltung bar ’gyur ro. This rendering follows the variant reading of S, which here has “awakening is not accessed” (byang chub la ma zhugs), rather than D: “entered the path of awakening” (byang chub lam zhugs). The Chinese concurs more with S, which makes more sense in the context; the Chinese does not have “path,” and instead reads: “[they] will hear this sūtra teaching that the awakening of all buddhas is not gained, not lost, beyond thought, beyond defilement, beyond illumination, concurs with thus, [but is] transmitted by the Buddha” (聞是經說諸佛菩提無得、無失、無有分別、無垢、無 明，隨順於如，佛所囑累。).

[n12] For this and the previous two paragraphs the translation remains tentative.

[n13] Tentative translation. D: bcom ldan ’das bdag gis dus ’gyur ba yang glo par ma chud cing bdag cag yun ji srid nas drangs pa’am / yun ji srid nas khrid pa yang skad cig gcig dang / thang cig gcig tsam yang glo bar ma chud la / yud tsam gcig kyang rjes su mi dran lags kyang bdag ni ’di snyam sems lags te.

[n14] The translation of this paragraph remains tentative.

[n15] We have not been able to find reference to this type of enumeration elsewhere.

[n16] Following C, J, N, K, Y, and H: rtun. D: rtul.

[n17] Following C, N, P, and Y: rin chen. D: rir chen.

[n18] Reading dgyes rather than bged.

[n19] The translation of these verses spoken by Aśoka remains tentative.

[n20] Following C, J, N, K, Y, and H: sems kyi. D: sems kyis.

[n21] Tentative translation. D: gang dag mig dang gzugs gnas shing // tshor ba dang ni ’du shes gnas // ’du byed la yang gnas nas su // bdag nyid rnam shes ma byas pa.

[n22] Tentative translation. D: bzod pa ’di ’dra de skye pa // blo gros bstan pas bzod du zad // bong ba’i chad pas mtshon chad la // de dag mi mjed can du ’gyur.

[n23] While each of the previous passages of this type have been listed in full, the text from this point on makes it clear that readers should infer a similar subject matter in the following abbreviated instances.

[n24] Following C, J, N, K, Y, and H: rgyal tshab nad yan. D: rgyal mtshan sa yan.

[n25] Although there is no exact indication of where the shift occurs, the speaker of the following verses at some point appears to change from being the emanated bodhisattvas to the Buddha Śākyamuni.

[n26] At this point the verses spoken by the bodhisattvas appear to end, such that the following verses are spoken by the Buddha.

[n27] Tentative translation. D: gang dag gcer bu’i sems can ma gtogs par // thos nas su zhig dga’ ba skye mi ’gyur // sangs rgyas kyis kyang de ni yong ma gsungs // ’on kyang de dag dge dang ldan par ’gyur.

[n28] Amogha (Tib. don yod) means “meaningful.”

[n29] The name “Infinite Armor” (go cha mtha’ yas) is repeated in the original text.

[n30] It is not quite clear which three classes are intended here. D: thub pa khams gsum nges ’byung rigs gsum ldan .

[n31] D: bag chags kyi mtsham sbyor ba ma lus pa nyid rjes su ’thob par ’gyur ba ste.

[n32] Tentative translation. D: de bzhin gshegs pas ’khor lo’i tshad tsam la gzigs na yang de lho nub kyi phyogs mtshams nas dpag tshad drug cu rtsa gnyis su sa yongs su g.yos par ’gyur ro.

[n33] Y, K, N, and H: na (“if”); D: nas (gerundive).

[n34] Y, K, N, and H: na (“if”); D: nas (gerundive).

[n35] Y, K, C, and U: nges (“conviction,” “certainty,” “ascertainment”); D: des (“gentleness,” “mildness”).

[n36] The translation of the following paragraph is tentative.

[n37] Y, K, N, and H: nges; D: des.

[n38] The translation of the final two lines of this verse is tentative. D: gang dag phug nas brten pa rnams/ /de dag gis ni lus mi shes.

[n39] According to MW. D: dha nu ska ri. The Mahāvyutpatti has dhānuṣkārī.

[n40] This perhaps refers to mandārava and mahāmandārava, which the Mahāvyutpatti lists consecutively.

[n41] Y, K, and H: rang gi; D: rang gis.

[n42] Y, J, K, N, C, and H: bstan (“teach”); D: brtan (“stable,” “stabilize”).

[n43] A more expanded analogy using the single taste of water collected in the ocean (but to illustrate slightly different points) can be seen at .

[n44] Translation of this verse is tentative. D: ji ltar rgyal srid rab bsngags na/ /bzhin ’dzun khro bar mi bgyis lags/ /de dag gi ni rnam rgyal der/ /sangs rgyas mthong ba’ang rnyed par ’gyur.

[n45] Literally “armor” (Tib. go cha, Skt. saṃnāha). Y, J, K, N, C, and H all have “procedure” (cho ga). We have translated based on D (go cha, “armor”) in light of its appearance in the passage immediately following.

[n46] gnyi ga’i cha las rnam par grol ba (ubhayato­bhāga­vimukta). Edgerton cites La Valle Poussin’s summary of the Abhidharmakośa’s interpretation of this phrase as “delivered from the obstacle of the passions (“impurities,” kleśāvaraṇa), and from the obstacle to (the eight) vimokṣa .”

[n47] J, N, C, and H: spyod par; D: sbyong bar; Y, K: spong bar.

[n48] Y, J, K, C, and H: gtong bar; N: gtang bar; D: gtod par.

[n49] Y, J, K, N, and C: gtor ba; D: gtod pa.

[n50] Y, J, N, and C: gtor bar; D: gtong bar; H: gtod par.

[n51] Y, K, and H: +mi.

[n52] There is a play on words here between “elements” (mahābhūta) and “unborn” (abhūta).

[n53] Y, J, K, N, and H: ma bsten; D: bsten.

[n54] Y, K, and H: ki; D: kyis.

[n55] Tentative translation. D: rtsa ’jings.

[n56] Y, K, N, C, U, and H: po; D: mo.

[n57] Tentative translation. D: bcom ldan ’das su sangs rgyas la skyabs su mi mchi/ chos la skyabs su mi mchi/ dge ’dun la skyabs su mi mchi ba des chos nyid de kun du ’tshal lags so.

[n58] Y, J, K, and C: de dag thams cad kyang rgya mtsho chen po rab tu gnas pa na nor bu rin po che de dag ni rin thang gdab du yod pa’am / rin thang gdab tu med pa yin pa de lta bur shes par bya ba yin zhing. N: de dag thams cad kyang rgya mtsho chen po na rab tu gnas pa na nor bu rin po che de dag ni rin thang gdab du yod pa’am / rin thang gdab tu med pa yin pa de lta bur shes par bya ba yin zhing.

[n59] U, H: gi; D: gis.

[n60] This is a poetic synonym for either “ocean” or “ground.” The term reappears below as an explicit epithet for “ocean.”

[n61] D: kun bged pa. This term is unattested in all lexicons, but present in several other texts of the Kangyur editions. Judging by the other contexts in which it appears, it might be related to the verb ’gyed = “to send,” “give,” “distribute,” “emanate,” or “argue.”

[n62] Y, J, K, N, C, and H: klog pa (Mahāvyutpatti = vācana: “to cause to recite,” “the act of recitation,” “reading,” “declaring”); D: zlog par (“to repeal, avert”).

[n63] Tentative translation. D: de tshe nor bu rnams kyi ’od ’byung ba/ /nor bu dag gi ’od du khyab par ’gyur.

[n64] Tentative translation. D: sha ra dva ti’ bu yang gang dag gzhan la phan pa’i phyir dang bdag la phan pa’i phyir zhugs pa dag lta zhog gi / sha ra dva ti’ bu sems can gang dag bdag dang gzhan la phan pa’i phyir zhugs pa de dag ni dkon no/ /mchog tu rab tu dkon no.

[n65] Y, K, and C: bral (“free from,” “separate from”); D: gral (“row”).

[n66] Y, K: ci bstan; J, N, and C: ji bstan (“what is taught”); D: ji bsten (“what is relied upon”).

[n67] Tentative translation. D: bcom ldan ’das slad kyis ni bcom ldan ’das las thos nas re zhig gang gis sems can ’ga’ yang bgyid pa de la ’jog pa’i mthu bdag bcag la ma mchis so.

[n68] rigs pa dang grol ba here and below describes two qualities of pratibhāna (spobs pa), “inspired speech,” or “eloquence,” which is a requisite quality of a qualified Dharma preacher: the ability to preach the Dharma in a “coherent” (yukta) and “free,” as in “fluid” and “fluent” (mukta), manner.

[n69] Y, K, N, and H: bsal; D: bstsal.

[n70] Y, K: chog (“sufficient”); D: mchog (“supreme”).

[n71] Tentative translation. D: bstan pa ’di ni brjod byas te/ /blo ngan dus ni drang po yin.

[n72] Tentative translation. D: ji ltar chags par blta bya dang/ /de yi gnas pa yod min bzhin.

[n73] N, C, and H: bsal; D: bstsal.

[n74] Tentative translation. D: yi ge ji bzhin phyag rgya grangs.

[n75] The translation of the first two lines of this verse is tentative. D: rab drag las can ser skya ljang ku skras/ /kas bub bum pa’i nang du rab tu ’jug.

[n76] The translation of the final two lines of this verse is tentative. D: de yi sems la nam yang ni/ /yongs su gdung ba byung ma gyur.

[n77] U, H: la. D: las.

[n78] Most available printings of the Degé Kangur have an error in the folio numbering from this point onward; the numbering error has been corrected in the displayed eKangyur pages but folio numbers in xylograph versions are likely to need increasing by one.

[n79] Y, K: las. D: la.

[n80] Y, J, K, N, C, and H: glo bur. D: blo bul. We have interpreted this term as a translation of āgantu (“guest”) rather than the more common akasmāt (“causeless,” “unforeseen,” “unexpected,” “sudden”).

[n81] The translation of this verse is tentative. D: byang chub spyad pa spyod pa dag kyang mthong/ /sangs rgyas zhing ’di ni ni dpa’ bog cig/ /gang zhig chos gos thogs nas gnas pa lags/ ma bslabs pa yis ’di la ji ltar bslab.

[n82] U, H: pa; D: pa’i.

[n83] Y, J, K, N, C, and H: tsam; D: snyam.

[n84] Tentative translation. D: brtan pa’i blo gros phyi ma’i tshe phyi ma’i dus lnga brgya pa tha ma la bab pa na/ gang las ting nge ’dzin de thos pa’i byang chub sems dpa’ de ni ting nge dzin des nges par ’byung ba yin zhing/ dge sbyong de’i spobs pa mtha’ yas pa yin par de’i mtha’ khong du chud par bya’o.

[n85] yul. Alternatively, this might be translated as “They fully know objects.”

[n86] The translation of the preceding three verses is tentative. D: gang gis de ni thob ’gyur ba’i/ ting ’dzin nga yis bshad pas na/ phyi nas ’chad pa su yi yang/ /bzhin la de ni lta mi ’gyur/ lha dang klu dang mi’am ci/ /mi dang mi ma yin rnams kyang/ bshad pas de yi gdong du lta/ /mang por rnam par lta bar ’gyur/ gang dag de yis gang nas thob/ de la des ni ji ltar bslabs/ ji ltar chos kyis khyad par ’phags/ mdo sde de ni rab bshad pas/ de dag bsam pa shes par ’gyur.

[n87] Y, J, K, N, C, and H: yi; D: yis.

[n88] The translation of the final two lines of this verse is tentative. D: dmigs pa’i rab tu dbye ba yis/ /ji ltar sprul pa ’byung ba bzhin.

[n89] Y and K are missing this line: kha cig byang chub phyir ni spyod snyam byed.

[n90] Y, J, K, N, C, and H: nga; D: de.
